01:38:07","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:07","title":"How the News Feed Algorithms Work on Facebook, Twitter & Instagram","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-algorithm-works-facebook-twitter-instagram","description":"<p>You're connected with hundreds of people — maybe even thousands — on Facebook, Twitter, and Instagram. But when you log in to each of these social networks, it's likely that you don't want to be bombarded by every single update from every single connection. That'd be pretty overwhelming, wouldn't it?</p> \n<p>That's how the folks from each of these social networks feel — and they've done plenty of user research to validate that feeling. In fact, that's exactly why the news feeds — and the algorithms behind them — exist.</p> \n<p>All three of today's most popular social networks have gravitated toward an algorithm-based feed in the effort to create better experiences for their users. The trouble is, each algorithm works differently. What's worse, they're constantly changing, making it hard for marketers like us to keep up.</p> \n<p>To help get it all straight, we've put together this simple guide on how the news feed works on the three most popular social networks: Facebook, Twitter, and Instagram. Let's dive in.</p> \n<p><strong>Note: </strong> Keep in mind that the algorithms are constantly changing. We'll continue to write about major social algorithm changes as they happen.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=3dc1dfd9-2cb4-4498-8c57-19dbb5671820&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Download Now: Social Media Trends in 2021 [Free Report]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/3dc1dfd9-2cb4-4498-8c57-19dbb5671820.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<h2>Facebook's News Feed Algorithm</h2> \n<p>Since the inception of the <a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/272014/global-social-networks-ranked-by-number-of-users/\">largest social media platform </a>to date, Facebook's news feed has been focused on personalizing the social media app's user experience. <a href=\"https://www.emarketer.com/content/social-networks-see-boosts-in-engagement-among-users-but-not-equally\">According to eMarketer</a>, we spend about 34 minutes each day using the platform.</p> \n<p>To give users the best experience possible, Facebook's team of engineers are constantly studying user behavior and picking up signals that show what kind of content each user is most interested in.</p> \n<h3>How It Works</h3> \n<p>The Like button has always been the epicenter of Facebook's user experience — not only because we see it on everyone's posts, but because it allows us to personalize our experience (and influence everyone else's). Since it was first introduced <a href=\"http://www.newstatesman.com/science-tech/social-media/2015/10/cursed-project-short-history-facebook-button\">in November 2007</a>, it's helped Facebook's engineers figure out which posts were delighting users, boring them, offending them, and so on.</p> \n<p>Nowadays, the algorithm that governs Facebook's News Feed has become much more sophisticated. It isn't just about the Like button anymore — and not just because <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/facebook-marketing\">reaction buttons are now in the mix</a>. In fact, Facebook's algorithm is by far the most complicated of the three social networks covered in this post.</p> \n<p>Here's a quick rundown of the most important things Facebook's algorithm takes into account.</p> \n<h4>Relevancy Score</h4> \n<p>When picking posts for each person who logs on to Facebook, the News Feed algorithm takes into account hundreds of variables — and can predict whether a given user will Like, click, comment, share, hide, or even mark a post as spam.</p> \n<p>More specifically, the algorithm predicts each of these outcomes with a certain degree of confidence. This prediction is quantified into a single number called a \"relevancy score\" that's specific both to you and to that post.</p> \n<p>Once every post that could potentially show up in your feed has been assigned a relevancy score, Facebook's sorting algorithm ranks them and puts them in the order they end up appearing in your feed. This means that every time you log in, the post you see at the top of your News Feed was chosen over thousands of others as the one most likely to make you react and engage.</p> \n<p>Ads are given relevancy scores, too, so that Facebook can show users the ads that could matter most to them. Again, this is supposed to give users a better experience — but it's also helpful for the businesses that are paying for the ads. It's calculated based on the positive feedback (video views, conversions, etc.) and negative feedback Facebook expects an ad to receive from its target audience. (Learn more about relevancy score for Facebook ads <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/business/news/relevance-score\">here</a>.)</p> \n<h4>Prioritizing Friends</h4> \n<p>Before 2015, Facebook was predicting what users want to see on the News Feed based on more indirect signals, like Likes, comments, and shares of others. Eventually, it <a href=\"http://newsroom.fb.com/news/2015/07/news-feed-fyi-a-better-understanding-of-hide/\">added options for users to filter out posts they don't want to see</a>. But what about helping boost the posts users do want to see?</p> \n<p>Through studies and surveys, Facebook found that many users were concerned about missing important updates from friends they cared about the most. In response to these concerns, the social media platform began changing the News Feed algorithm to give more control to the users themselves.</p> \n<p>It started <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-updates-news-feed-algorithm?_ga=1.105819395.1866822358.1456501228\">in April 2015</a>, when the company began giving priority (in the form of higher relevancy scores) to posts from friends over the Pages they follow and promotional posts. Later that year, in July, Facebook <a href=\"http://newsroom.fb.com/news/2015/07/updated-controls-for-news-feed/\">introduced the \"See First\" feature</a>, which lets you actually hand-pick which accounts — whether friends or followed Pages — you want to see first at the top of your News Feed.</p> \n<p>Now, when you want to prioritize a person or page to \"see first,\" their posts will appear at the top of your News Feed. To prioritize the people or pages you want to \"see first\": click the <strong>downward facing arrow</strong> in the top-right corner of any Facebook page and select <strong>Settings</strong>.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Set up the see first feature in Facebook\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20the%20News%20Feed%20Algorithms%20Work%20on%20Facebook,%20Twitter%20%26%20Instagram-1.png?width=400&amp;name=How%20the%20News%20Feed%20Algorithms%20Work%20on%20Facebook,%20Twitter%20%26%20Instagram-1.png\" title=\"\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\"></p> \n<p>In the window that appears, scroll until you find <span style=\"font-weight: bold;\">News Feed Preferences</span> and select it.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Facebook newsfeed preferences\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20the%20News%20Feed%20Algorithms%20Work%20on%20Facebook,%20Twitter%20%26%20Instagram.png?width=400&amp;name=How%20the%20News%20Feed%20Algorithms%20Work%20on%20Facebook,%20Twitter%20%26%20Instagram.png\" title=\"\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\"></p> \n<p>Next, select <span style=\"font-weight: bold;\">Prioritize who to see first</span>.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"prioritize who to see first in facebook\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20the%20News%20Feed%20Algorithms%20Work%20on%20Facebook,%20Twitter%20%26%20Instagram-3.png?width=400&amp;name=How%20the%20News%20Feed%20Algorithms%20Work%20on%20Facebook,%20Twitter%20%26%20Instagram-3.png\" title=\"\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\"></p> \n<p>Finally, select up to 30 of your Facebook friends to add as favorites. You'll now see posts from these individuals first.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"add friends to facebook favorities\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20the%20News%20Feed%20Algorithms%20Work%20on%20Facebook,%20Twitter%20%26%20Instagram-2.png?width=400&amp;name=How%20the%20News%20Feed%20Algorithms%20Work%20on%20Facebook,%20Twitter%20%26%20Instagram-2.png\" title=\"\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\"></p> \n<h4>Time Spent on a Post</h4> \n<p>Facebook started monitoring how much time users spend viewing certain posts. Of course, the time you spend on a post can vary depending on your internet speed, the length of the post, and so on — and the folks at Facebook are aware of that.</p> \n<p>However, the platform's strategists found that <a href=\"https://glean.info/dwell-time-a-rising-metric-for-social-media-seo-content-marketing/#:~:text=More%20specifically%2C%20dwell%20time%20is,Yext%2C%20in%20Search%20Engine%20Journal.\">dwell time</a>, the act of spending a lot more time on a particular post in their feed compared to the majority of other posts they look at, is a good sign that the content was relevant to them.</p> \n<p>How does this play out in the feed? If you spend more time on a particular post, <a href=\"http://wallaroomedia.com/facebook-newsfeed-algorithm-change-history/\">Facebook is more likely </a>to show that post on your friends' News Feeds.</p> \n<h4>Video Engagement</h4> \n<p>In summer 2015, Facebook surveyed users on how they interacted with video on their News Feeds and found that that many people who were interested in a given video didn't necessarily Like it, comment on it, or share it with their friends. Since engagement is one of the primary ways Facebook measures people's interest in posts, it had to come up with other ways to figure out whether people enjoyed the videos they were seeing.</p> \n<p>To do that, the company started monitoring other forms of video engagement — like turning on the audio, switching to full-screen mode, or enabling high definition. So if you turn up the volume on a video or make it full-screen, the algorithm will interpret that as you enjoying the video, and will show you similar videos higher up in your feed.</p> \n<p>The update doesn't mean users will see more videos in their News Feed — only those who already engage more with video-related content.</p> \n<p>Facebook's algorithm is very, very complex, but we hope that gives you a good idea of what it considers important so you can tweak your <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/facebook-marketing?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-algorithm-works-facebook-twitter-instagram&amp;hubs_post-cta=Facebook%20marketing\">Facebook marketing </a>strategy accordingly. Now, let's move on to Twitter.</p> \n<h2>Twitter's Timeline Algorithm</h2> \n<p>Whereas Facebook makes most of the decisions about what will show up in your Facebook News Feed, Twitter's historically taken a very different approach with what it calls the \"Timeline.\"</p> \n<p>Your Timeline is the stream of tweets from the users you follow that shows up on your account home page when you first log in. It used to be that your Timeline was made up of every single tweet from every user you follow, in chronological order. But the folks at Twitter found that, similarly to what was happening on Facebook, users felt they were missing all the best tweets from the people they care about most.</p> \n<p>The changes made to the Twitter algorithm aren't nearly as platform-changing as the ones Facebook have made, but they are somewhat of a departure from the real-time element that has defined Twitter since the beginning.</p> \n<h3>How It Works</h3> \n<p>The engineers at Twitter have attempted two different approaches for surfacing the \"best\" tweets first on your Timeline: the \"While You Were Away\" feature and the even newer \"Show me the best Tweets first\" feature.</p> \n<h4>The \"While You Were Away\" Feature</h4> \n<p>This feature was added as an attempt to rid users of whatever FOMO (fear of missing out) they might have been feeling from the chronological nature of the original Timeline.</p> \n<p>Basically, it's a recap of some of the best tweets you may not have seen otherwise. How do these tweets make the cut? It's determined by \"user engagement\".</p> \n<p>You can't turn off the feature, but how often you see it depends on how often you use Twitter. The recaps pop up more frequently for users who check the app less often.</p> \n<h4>The \"Show Me the Best Tweets First\" Feature</h4> \n<p>The \"Show me the best Tweets first\" feature is a little more similar to Facebook's News Feed. Why? Because it actually changes the content on your Timeline based on a tweet's relevancy, rather than listing tweets chronologically.</p> \n<p>By default, Twitter's algorithm puts the tweets it thinks you'll find most interesting at the top of your Timeline, these posts are still recent and in reverse chronological order. These tweets are chosen based on accounts you interact with most, tweets you engage with, and much more.</p> \n<h4>The \"Best Tweets\" Feature</h4> \n<p>The rest of the tweets will be displayed right underneath, also in reverse chronological order. Unlike the \"While you were away\" feature, these \"best tweets\" won't be highlighted or indicated in any way — so you won't be able to tell where the \"best tweets\" stop and the rest of the tweets begin.</p> \n<p>There are two ways to remove these \"best tweets\" from the top of your Timeline. One is a quick fix: You can always refresh your Timeline to see all new tweets at the top in the live way you might have been used to seeing in the past.</p> \n<p>But if you want to always see your Timeline live, then Twitter does allow you to opt out of this feature if you'd like — unlike Facebook's News Feed.</p> \n<p>To opt out of this feature: Tap the three-star iconin the top right corner of your screen. Then tap Switch to latest Tweets.</p> \n<h3><img alt=\"Set your Twitter timeline to see latest tweets first\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20the%20News%20Feed%20Algorithms%20Work%20on%20Facebook,%20Twitter%20%26%20Instagram-4.png?width=400&amp;name=How%20the%20News%20Feed%20Algorithms%20Work%20on%20Facebook,%20Twitter%20%26%20Instagram-4.png\" title=\"\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\"></h3> \n<h3>Is Twitter Moving Away From a Real-Time Timeline?</h3> \n<p>There's no reason to believe so — at least not right now. One of the three sections of your Twitter timeline is composed of tweets displayed in reverse-chronological order. After you scroll through the \"While you were away\" Tweets and \"Best Tweets\" you'll be left with the tweets from your followers starting with the most recent.</p> \n<p>What might be an emerging trend on Twitter is the opportunity to <a href=\"https://www.newsweek.com/twitter-reacts-super-follows-subscription-feature-riptwitter-1572262\">subscribe to people's tweets</a>. While this feature wouldn't disrupt the timeline's mostly reverse-chronological order, it could add just one more section to your feed that you'll need to scroll through before seeing the latest updates from your followers.</p> \n<p>Twitter isn't the only social media platform iterating its algorithm to show the most interesting content first — Instagram's algorithm is giving Facebook and Twitter a run for their money.</p> \n<h2>The Instagram Feed's Algorithm</h2> \n<p>As of January 2021, Instagram has more than <a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/272014/global-social-networks-ranked-by-number-of-users/\">1.2 million active users </a>on the platform making it a <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/instagram-marketing\">hotspot for marketers </a>in nearly any industry. However, it's a newer platform compared to the other two on this list, so many of us marketers are still trying to figure it out. The best place to start is from the bottom up — with the algorithm.</p> \n<p>Instagram's algorithm has evolved since 2016 when it first began sorting users' news feeds in order of relevance rather than recency. Now, the algorithm works similarly to its parent company's — Facebook. Using machine learning to aggregate six factors, Instagram can determine what content you'll appreciate the most and influence your news feed to prioritize that content.</p> \n<p>These six factors shared by <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/06/01/how-instagram-feed-works/\">TechCrunch </a>are:</p> \n<p><strong>Interest:</strong> This is a prediction Instagram makes about how interested you'll be in a particular post.</p> \n<p><strong>Frequency:</strong> How often you use the app that will determine what posts you see first when you open the app again.</p> \n<p><strong>Following:</strong> The more people you follow, the less likely you'll be able to see everyone in your news feed.</p> \n<p><strong>Recency:</strong> How recently was a post published? This impacts when you'll see a post in your news feed.</p> \n<p><strong>Relationship:</strong> Who shared the post and your connection to them will be a significant factor in how often you'll see their content. This is influenced by tagged photos, engagement, and even how often you direct message them.</p> \n<p><strong>Usage:</strong> The time you spend on Instagram affects the content you see as well.</p> \n<h3>What about the Reels, Shop, and Explore pages?</h3> \n<p>With the advent of Reels, Shop, and the Explore page, there are several opportunities for Instagram users to naturally affect the factors listed above by interacting with content outside of their news feeds. If you enjoy cooking videos, for example, you may see more of those types of videos and reels in your news feed.</p> \n<h3>Is Instagram removing likes?</h3> \n<p>We'd be remiss if we didn't mention the latest Instagram algorithm update in the works — <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/instagram-to-test-hiding-like-counts-in-us-wired25-2019-11\">removing likes</a>. Removing one of the most popular features of the app is being tested right now as a measure <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2019/12/06/instagram-hiding-likes-could-increase-post-volume.html\">against bullying and increased pressure </a>to post content that garners more and more social approval for young Instagrammers.</p> \n<p>The change has already taken effect in several countries including Canada, Brazil, and Australia. While it hasn't made its way to the United States in a widespread way yet, don't get too comfortable with your news feed engagement appearing for all to see. There could soon come a time when only you will see how many likes your posts receive.</p> \n<h2>It's All About Content Quality</h2> \n<p>The key takeaway for brands and individuals alike is this: Quality is Queen.</p> \n<p>These algorithms are meant to filter out irrelevant and poor-quality posts so that the highest-quality content gets through. Control over what users see and don't see is a collaboration between the social platform and the user. The user interacts with what they find interesting and the social media platform takes note and shows you more of that the next time you open the app.</p> \n<p>The big lesson for Facebook, Twitter, and Instagram marketers like us is to remember that it's our job to post content to social that's interesting, entertaining, helpful, and/or relevant to our audiences. This means picking relevant topics, writing delightful copy, and posting compelling images and videos.</p> \n<p>By following these best practices, your posts will have a better chance of getting shown to users — so you can continue to inspire, delight, and educate them.</p> \n<p><em>Editor's note: This post was originally published in April 2016 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.</em></p> 01:38:07","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:07","title":"Why P2P Marketing Might Be a Good Alternative to Influencer Marketing","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/p2p-marketing","description":"<p>To understand what peer-to-peer (P2P) marketing is, let's start with an example.</p> \n<p>Recently, I was looking for a new face moisturizer. Of course, I <em>could've</em>&nbsp;trusted the numerous influencers I follow on Instagram, all with strong opinions regarding the \"best, most effective\"<em>&nbsp;</em>options available.</p> \n<p>But I wasn't convinced these influencers had my best interest in-mind. Yes, most influencers' (and micro-influencers) are successful because they promote valuable products. But they're getting commission off those posts, too.</p> \n<p>So I handled my problem the old-fashioned way — I texted my friends and asked what products they use.</p> \n<p>This isn't to say influencer marketing is ineffective. Quite the opposite: When done right, influencer marketing is a fantastic opportunity to expand your brand's reach and increase sales.</p> \n<p>But depending on your team's budget, influencer marketing could be limiting. Plus, influencer marketing inhibits your brand from reaching those consumers who still trust their peers above all else.</p> \n<p>Enter: P2P marketing.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=814dd420-0d49-40e0-b59c-f01066e186c1&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Download Now: Free Brand Building Guide\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/814dd420-0d49-40e0-b59c-f01066e186c1.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p>Given <a href=\"https://www.marketingcharts.com/cross-media-and-traditional/word-of-mouth-113276\">93% of consumers trust friends and family</a>&nbsp;over all other influences (including review sites, blogs, and social media platforms), it makes sense why P2P marketing works.</p> \n<p>And P2P marketing, a form of <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/agency/how-online-word-of-mouth-marketing-is-changing\">word-of-mouth marketing</a>, isn't new. People have been giving personal opinions about their favorite — and least favorite — brands, products, and services long before social media.</p> \n<p>Some older forms of P2P marketing include Yelp, reviews on personal business' websites, and good old-fashioned conversations between your consumers and their friends and family.</p> \n<p>However, there are some new tools that help businesses leverage P2P marketing on a broader scale. <a href=\"https://amazingbrands.io/clients/\">Amazing Brands</a>, for instance, helps businesses generate customer reviews and referrals, guarantee event attendance, or even increase in-store foot traffic.</p> \n<p>The tool ultimately relies on the premise of P2P marketing, which is that there's nothing more powerful than peer recommendations.</p> \n<p>Other tools, like <a href=\"https://www.higherlogic.com/\">Higher Logic</a>, work to establish a sense of community among existing consumers, and increase brand loyalty — a critical component of P2P marketing. (Since consumers won't refer products or services towards which they don't feel loyal.)</p> \n<p>However, if you're learning about P2P marketing for the first time, you might be wondering — why invest in P2P marketing, instead of more traditional forms of influencer marketing?</p> \n<p>And what's the difference, anyway?&nbsp;</p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">What's the difference between P2P marketing and influencer marketing?</h3> \n<p>Over the past couple years, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-work-with-influencers\">influencer marketing has been one of the most popular</a> and effective opportunities for brands to reach new audiences by leveraging those influencers' built-in communities.</p> \n<p>However, as mentioned above, consumers still trust their own peers more than anyone else. And influencers can often feel like celebrities to the general public — in fact, sometimes, they <em>are </em>actual celebrities, like <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-work-with-influencers\">George Clooney with Nespresso</a>. This removes a level of authenticity you might be striving for as a brand.</p> \n<p>Additionally, many small and medium-sized businesses can't afford the typical influencer cost. Celebrity or macro-influencers charge between <a href=\"https://cdn2.hubspot.net/hubfs/53/Sprout%20Social/hubspot-influencer-marketing-guide%20(1).pdf?__hstc=233546881.b08a0971055865ab76da45b879eff11f.1616195018855.1616195018855.1616195018855.1&amp;__hssc=233546881.1.1616195018855&amp;__hsfp=3521948877#:~:text=To%20get%20a%20gauge%20on,%243%2C000%2D500%2C000%2B%20per%20post.\">$3,000 and $500,000 for a single post</a>&nbsp;— and while micro-influencers are undoubtedly cheaper, they can also charge upwards of <a href=\"https://cdn2.hubspot.net/hubfs/53/Sprout%20Social/hubspot-influencer-marketing-guide%20(1).pdf?__hstc=20629287.0c93a60d870574892216af66c4084de1.1565290736946.1570715862629.1570889361716.32&amp;__hssc=20629287.3.1570889361716&amp;__hsfp=1688475938#:~:text=To%20get%20a%20gauge%20on,%243%2C000%2D500%2C000%2B%20per%20post.\">$500 per post</a>.</p> \n<blockquote> \n <p><span style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Ultimately, P2P is a form of marketing that can feel increasingly trustworthy and authentic through real, genuine reviews from peers who have no incentive to promote businesses they don't care about. </span></p> \n</blockquote> \n<p>To further explore the difference between P2P marketing and influencer marketing, let's consider an example.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>Jessica Alba's business, The Honest Company, has a <a href=\"https://www.referwise.com/invite-friends-earn-20-with-honest-referral-program/\">referral program in which they credit existing customers $20</a> for each invited friend who makes a purchase.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>This is an example of P2P marketing.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>Influencer marketing, on the other hand, refers to the influencers on Instagram (as well as other social platforms) who <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/explore/tags/honestambassador/\">tag posts with #honestambassador</a>, signifying the post is sponsored by The Honest Company.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>These are both equally valuable marketing options, but they achieve different goals. The P2P marketing initiative (in this case, the referral program), aims to tap into The Honest Company's existing consumers to reach new prospects.</p> \n<p>The P2P program is likely more narrow in reach, but has the potential to convert more quickly than influencer marketing, since it's leveraging the power of an existing relationship between customers and their friends or family.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>The influencer marketing program, alternatively, is meant to spread brand awareness about Honest Company to a wider audience.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>P2P marketing can take many different forms depending on your brand and business goals — including creating a referral program, encouraging reviews on your site in exchange for a small discount or prize, or organizing events meant to increase brand awareness to the larger community.</p> \n<p>Ultimately, P2P marketing comes down to increasing the incentive for your consumers to share your product or service with friends and family, which is undoubtedly one of the best long-term strategies for success.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=ddbf2eb7-04e8-44b2-9e05-b21264e09b65&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"New Call-to-action\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/ddbf2eb7-04e8-44b2-9e05-b21264e09b65.png\"></a></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fp2p-marketing&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 05 Apr 2021 11:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/814dd420-0d49-40e0-b59c-f01066e186c1.png","linkMd5":"53238816fd2a2fd09ddd186c47d41aaa","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn67@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-07-749_eac7fa40866dc905.webp","destWidth":382,"destHeight":59,"sourceBytes":4555,"destBytes":6088,"author":"Caroline Forsey","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/814dd420-0d49-40e0-b59c-f01066e186c1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn67@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-07-749_eac7fa40866dc905.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/ddbf2eb7-04e8-44b2-9e05-b21264e09b65.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn34@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-14-301_f4156d3bc1379fd0.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fp2p-marketing&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn52@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-15-334_a6931be2aa72280b.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817087174},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:07","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:07","title":"Five Lessons I Learned About Scaling a Business With Reid Hoffman","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/mindset-of-scale-lessons","description":"<p>How great would it be if you had a panel of successful entrepreneurs and business leaders you could turn to whenever you needed help getting unstuck, or needed a daily dose of inspiration?</p>  \n<p>Fortunately, that's exactly what the new Masters of Scale Courses App offers — expert advice from some of the world's best and brightest minds, guided by Reid Hoffman.</p> \n<p>The first course is all about The Mindset of Scale. Here's what I learned from the first two lessons.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=e9d2eacb-6b01-423a-bf7a-19d42ba77eaa&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"→ Download Now: Free Business Plan Template\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/e9d2eacb-6b01-423a-bf7a-19d42ba77eaa.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<h3><strong>1. Ask \"Why not?\" and \"What if?\"</strong></h3> \n<p>Start by asking two important questions — \"Why not?\" and \"What if?\" — whenever you encounter something that makes you feel a strong emotion.</p> \n<p>For instance, think about the last time you experienced sticker shock or frustration over waiting in a long line. Those simple questions have sparked countless successful products and businesses — including Virgin Airlines. In his own words, here's Richard Branson:</p> \n<p>\"35 years ago, when we started [Virgin Airlines], the big carriers were dreadful. And<span style=\"text-decoration: line-through; color: #cccccc;\">&nbsp;</span>on one of those flights coming to the Virgin Islands, I got bumped, which is a sort of typical thing that airlines did in those days.\"</p> \n<p>Of course, being Richard Branson, he didn't pass the time by staring woefully at the departures board. Instead, he asked one of those powerful questions: <em>What if? What if he didn't have to wait for the next flight? What if he created a flight of his own?</em></p> \n<p>\"So I hired a plane and filled it up with all the people who had been bumped and called it Virgin Airlines as a joke. And we arrived in the BVI, and during that flight, I just thought, 'Airlines do bump people, maybe I should ring up Boeing the next day.' Which I did, and asked if they had any secondhand 747s for sale.\"</p> \n<p>As you can probably guess, they did, and Virgin Airways was born. Now, you may not be in the market for used 747 jets, but that doesn't mean these questions can't create similarly impactful results for you. So next time you find yourself feeling any powerful emotion, pause for a second, think about the situation, and ask yourself, \"What if?\"</p> \n<h3><strong>2. Have an idea, act on it, and never look back.</strong></h3> \n<p>Even though many people talk about the power of ideas, what the world actually rewards is action.</p> \n<p>Generating ideas is often the easy part — and with the right mindset, it's a process that can become second nature. But, what separates daydreaming from living your dream is taking action.</p> \n<p>Richard Branson has been an entrepreneur since he was 14 and launched his first business: a student magazine. After the magazine, he went on to found a record label, a video game publisher, and many other ventures — each one a product of taking action.</p> \n<p>If you're like me, even just reading that list of accomplishments sounds daunting. To overcome that feeling, Reid Hoffman offers this helpful advice: \"Next time you have an idea that you can't stop thinking about,<span style=\"text-decoration: line-through; color: #b7b7b7;\">&nbsp;</span>act on it immediately.\"</p> \n<p>After asking yourself \"Why not?\" or \"What if?\", identify the smallest or most immediate action you can do right now to act on your idea.</p> \n<p>By starting small and taking action right away, you can avoid the dreaded \"analysis paralysis\" and start building momentum towards your goal instead.</p> \n<h3><strong>3. Need a big idea? Get intentional about looking for one.</strong></h3> \n<p>Before founding Spanx, Sarah Blakely was stuck in a dead-end job — making door-to-door fax machine sales were far from fulfilling. She knew she wasn't on the right path, but she just wasn't sure what that right path looked like.</p> \n<p>After a challenging day, she decided to try something different. In her journal, she wrote down, \"I want to invent a product that I can sell to millions of people that will make them feel good.\" According to Blakely, \"This was something that I set an intention for; I had really asked the universe to give me an idea that I could bring to the world.\"</p> \n<p>Blakely kept asking herself, \"Is this my big idea?\" until the answer was \"Yes.\"</p> \n<p>With her newfound intention, Blakely began finding the opportunities and ideas all around her. One night, after getting frustrated with her undergarment options, she cut the feet off of her pantyhose and discovered that her DIY solution was exactly what she was looking for — in more ways than one.</p> \n<h3><strong>4. Fill knowledge gaps with the people around you.</strong></h3> \n<p>After discovering her big idea for Spanx, Blakely faced a new challenge: How to build a business in an industry she knew almost nothing about. It wasn't an easy problem to solve, but Blakely wasn't about to let a lack of domain expertise get in her way.</p> \n<p>Instead, she started digging deeper. In the words of Reid Hoffman, \"She knew that to succeed, she had to be continually open to information and ideas — always in search of the insights and people who could help her turn her idea into a reality.\"</p> \n<p>It's okay not to know everything about your business, as long as you get help from people who can fill in your knowledge gaps. You'll go faster and further with the help of other people.</p> \n<p>Ask lots of questions to find your idea — and then keep asking them.</p> \n<h3><strong>5. Find a place or time where you do your best thinking, and set aside time to be in that space.</strong></h3> \n<p>Creating a successful business, launching a new product or campaign, or just keeping up with a highly demanding job all require a lot of decision-making. And good decision-making rests on a foundation of good thinking.</p> \n<p>According to Hoffman, \"Wherever, whenever and however, the point is this: an idea won't come looking for you, and it won't perfect itself. You have to put yourself in spaces and places and frames of mind, where you can find and shape the idea.\"</p> \n<p>For more lessons about scale, download the Masters of Scale Courses app for 50% using the code <span style=\"color: #222222;\">HUBSPOT at</span>&nbsp;<a href=\"https://account.mastersofscale.com/membership?utm_source=Hubspot&amp;utm_medium=Email&amp;utm_campaign=HUBSPOT\">join.mastersoscale.com/hubstpot</a>. <em>Offer is valid through 5/15/21.</em>&nbsp;</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=9ce704de-19f2-4fd0-8041-22dc3c021b87&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"Business Plan Template\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/9ce704de-19f2-4fd0-8041-22dc3c021b87.png\"></a></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fmindset-of-scale-lessons&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 06 Apr 2021 11:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/e9d2eacb-6b01-423a-bf7a-19d42ba77eaa.png","linkMd5":"423135fd2946c04628076715ab28526f","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn60@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-07-771_8ff1ce58a24f6d9c.webp","destWidth":428,"destHeight":59,"sourceBytes":4856,"destBytes":6606,"author":"acollins@hubspot.com (Alicia Collins)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/e9d2eacb-6b01-423a-bf7a-19d42ba77eaa.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn60@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-07-771_8ff1ce58a24f6d9c.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/9ce704de-19f2-4fd0-8041-22dc3c021b87.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn92@2020_6/2021/04/07/17-38-14-653_ec9e2c896a128892.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fmindset-of-scale-lessons&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn43@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-15-218_66180e35b03d2184.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817087144},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:07","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:07","title":"7 Tips for Designing a Social Media Page That Stands Out","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/social-media-design","description":"<p>At least once a month, I discover a new brand and take a quick peek at their profile. Within a few seconds, I decide if I'll hit that \"follow\" button or exit the page.</p>  \n<p>In those few seconds that I'm assessing the brand's profile, I'm asking myself two questions: Is their content visually appealing and am I interested in the type of content they will be posting?</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=6b90aadb-dd8c-4687-89a3-c245110c6a91&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"→ Download Now: 50+ Free Social Media Image Templates\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/6b90aadb-dd8c-4687-89a3-c245110c6a91.png\"></a></p> \n<p>I'd bet many social media users take a similar approach. This is why social media design is an instrumental part of your social strategy. So much of social media is about perception and design plays a big role in determining that.</p> \n<p>How can you make sure your design attracts the right audience? We'll cover that and more below.</p> \n<p>Nowadays, social platforms are often the first place consumers discover brands. As such, making a great first impression is the first step to building a robust <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/blog/tabid/6307/bid/4663/how-to-monitor-your-social-media-presence-in-10-minutes-a-day.aspx\">social media presence</a>.</p> \n<p>Your social media design will also impact your brand perception. Every post you create and publish tells a story and contributes to your brand image. You want to make sure that story aligns with your overall messaging and builds a connection with your audience.</p> \n<p>This is particularly important on platforms that prioritize visuals, like <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/instagram-for-business-guide\">Instagram</a>, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/tiktok-for-business\">TikTok</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/facebook-marketing\">Facebook</a>. But you'll still need to make sure your designs are consistent on all platforms.</p> \n<h2>What to Consider For Social Media Post Designs</h2> \n<p>Before you start working on your design, you'll want to consider a few things. The first is your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/branding\">brand identity</a> – your social media platform will be the visual representation of it, so you and your team must have a clear idea of what it is.</p> \n<p>The next step is conducting <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/market-research-buyers-journey-guide\">market research </a>to understand your audience. Questions to answer include:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>What are they looking for in a brand?</li> \n <li>What are their values?</li> \n <li>What are they interested in?</li> \n <li>What are they concerned about?</li> \n <li>What do they like to see on social media? What do they like to see on X platform?</li> \n</ul> \n<p>This will serve as your frame of reference to drive your design approach.</p> \n<p>You'll then want to look at your competition's designs. While you have your unique approach, it's useful to know what visual strategies they're using and how consumers are responding. The more information you have, the better equipped you will be to design creative assets that resonate with your audience.</p> \n<h2>Tips For Designing Social Media Posts</h2> \n<h3>1. Aim for consistency and cohesion.</h3> \n<p>Consistency is key when designing your social media page. Why? Because it helps with brand recognition.</p> \n<p>Imagine if every time you saw a brand, they changed their brand colors and logo. You would probably confuse it for another brand or forget it altogether. Brand recognition is important for building trust and loyalty with your audience.</p> \n<p>Beyond posting regularly, consistency on social media also means sticking to a visual theme. Is it dark and moody or light and airy? Do you want your page to evoke calm, excitement, balance, focus, or something else?</p> \n<p>Whatever your answers are to those questions should be reflected in a cohesive design. One way to do this is by using the same filter or editing style on all of your images to ensure they all fit within your branding.</p> \n<h3>2. Use colors to mirror your brand identity.</h3> \n<p>It's no surprise that colors affect how consumers perceive your brand. That's why popular food brands are usually associated with the colors red and yellow, and financial institutions with blues.</p> \n<p>There are a few ways to incorporate color into your social media design. The first is in your templates. If you plan to use templates when posting graphics, you'll want to incorporate your colors to increase your brand recognition.</p> \n<p>For your images and videos, you can also highlight certain colors to stand out.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"Urban Skin instagram page\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/8%20Tips%20for%20Designing%20Your%20Social%20Media.png?width=250&amp;name=8%20Tips%20for%20Designing%20Your%20Social%20Media.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 250px;\" title=\"\" width=\"250\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"http://instagram.com/urbanskinrx\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>In the example above, Urban Skin consistently uses two main colors in its design: peach and turquoise. While they may have other colors in their images, these two are always front and center.</p> \n<p>Another strategy is designing your social media posts to align with a particular theme and color. For instance, let's say you're a fashion brand and you're planning February content. Given the association of February with Valentine's Day and the color red, you could build your creative assets around that theme for the month.</p> \n<h3>3. Use social media design templates.</h3> \n<p>If you want to scale your social media strategy, you'll likely need to have templates.</p> \n<p>They're a huge time saver and ensure consistent branding. Platforms like <a href=\"http://canva.com\">Canva</a> make it easy for teams to create and share templates that have been approved by the branding team and align with your strategy. Jump to that section [here].</p> \n<p>Be sure to have a diverse set of templates that can be used for various content types, such as infographics and videos. For instance, this brand <a href=\"https://mateonewyork.com/\">Mateo New York</a> likely uses templates that produce a sleek and attractive layout that stays consistent.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"Mateo New York instagram design \" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/8%20Tips%20for%20Designing%20Your%20Social%20Media.jpeg?width=250&amp;name=8%20Tips%20for%20Designing%20Your%20Social%20Media.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 250px;\" title=\"\" width=\"250\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"http://instagram.com/mateonewyork\">Image Source</a></p> \n<h3>4. Adapt your design to the platform.</h3> \n<p>Every platform has different sizing and content guidelines.</p> \n<p>For example, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/instagram-reels\">Instagram Reels</a> are formatted to be viewed on smartphones, which means videos must be filmed in portrait orientation. Facebook, on the other hand, is formatted for landscape videos – similar to YouTube.</p> \n<p>For videos in particular, you want to avoid having content with black sidebars, as that isn't visually appealing.</p> \n<p>Beyond sizing, you also have to consider which platforms are appropriate for certain designs. For instance, an infographic probably wouldn't do well on Twitter. Breaking that content down into a text thread is a better strategy.</p> \n<p>Following these guidelines will make your content more likely to perform well.</p> \n<h3>5. Follow design best practices.</h3> \n<p>The main goal of your social media design is to create visually appealing content that captures your audience's attention and encourages them to engage.</p> \n<p>While several factors influence this, there are general design rules that are known to create appealing visuals. The first is white or negative space, which is when an area in your frame is left empty. Using white or negative space helps draw the eye to what you want your audience to focus on.</p> \n<iframe style=\"margin: 0px auto; display: block;\" src=\"https://assets.pinterest.com/ext/embed.html?id=459226493254000644\" width=\"345\" height=\"618\" frameborder=\"0\"></iframe> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.yvonnekone.com/\">Yvonne Koné </a>uses white space in its social media design, which reflects the brand's simplistic and minimalist identity.</p> \n<p>Here are a few other <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/design\">design principles</a> you'll want to consider when developing your creative assets:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Hierarchy </strong>– Arranging your visual elements by order of importance. You can do this by playing around with sizing, contrast, space, and other elements.</li> \n <li><strong>Balance </strong>– Having equal visual weight in an image, which creates harmony, like <a href=\"https://twitter.com/LonezScents/status/1333518401894043652/photo/1\">in this example</a>.</li> \n <li><strong>Contrast </strong>– Putting elements with opposite colors, sizes, or textures to make them stand out.</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>6. Don't forget about your profile.</h3> \n<p>While the main focus will be on your social media posts, don't forget to design your social profiles.</p> \n<p>Your profile picture, cover photo, and other visual elements should be a top priority when designing your social media. Here are some tips to follow:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Be sure to use the same profile picture, i.e. your logo, on all social platforms.</li> \n <li>Use a cover photo that aligns both visually and contextually with your brand.</li> \n <li>Only update your profile to highlight events or holidays that are important to your brand. For instance, some brands add a rainbow pride flag to their logo in June in solidarity with the LGBTQ community.</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>7. Rely on creative professionals.</h3> \n<p>Your social media design will only be as good as your investment.</p> \n<p>When it comes to images and illustrations, it's worth consulting professionals who specialize in creating high-quality content. They can guide you through the creative process and make suggestions that will elevate your design.</p> \n<p>If your team cannot invest in a full-time creative, consider independent contractors. With this approach, you can work on a project-by-project basis and experiment with different designers.</p> \n<h2>How To Find Social Media Design Templates</h2> \n<p>If your team wants an easy way to source templates, there's a cost-effective way to do so without sacrificing quality. Many online branding companies offer customizable templates that have been designed by professionals. Here are a few to consider:</p> \n<h3>1. Canva</h3> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.canva.com/\">Canva</a> is a graphic design platform with over 250,000 free templates available for personal and commercial use.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"Canva homepage\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/8%20Tips%20for%20Designing%20Your%20Social%20Media-2.png?width=600&amp;name=8%20Tips%20for%20Designing%20Your%20Social%20Media-2.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 600px;\" title=\"\" width=\"600\"></p> \n<p>In addition to templates, Canva also has an extensive stock library with photos, animations, and videos for brands in any industry. The platform is free for individual users and has professional and enterprise options for larger companies, with pricing going up to $30/month.</p> \n<h3>2. Lucidpress</h3> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.lucidpress.com/pages/\">Lucidpress</a> is a brand templating platform that makes it easy to create everything from social media posts to ebooks.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"Lucidpress homepage\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/8%20Tips%20for%20Designing%20Your%20Social%20Media-1.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<p>The platform is free to start using. To gain access to unlimited templates, pricing starts at $10 a month and can go up depending on your business needs.</p> \n<p>Your branding doesn't stop at your logo or website. It also extends to your social media. By investing time to develop a brand-specific social media design, you will get one step closer to connecting with your target audience.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" 01:38:07","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:07","title":"Paid Social Media: Worth The Investment?","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/paid-social-media","description":"<p>Social media advertising spend is expected to top <a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/246341/social-media-advertising-spending-in-the-us/#:~:text=In%202021%2C%20social%20media%20advertising,spending%20forecast%20for%20that%20year.\">$47.9 billion in 2021</a>. That’s nearly 20% of the total <a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/429036/advertising-expenditure-in-north-america/#:~:text=It%20was%20calculated%20that%20the,by%20the%20end%20of%202022.\">expected advertising spend</a> by all North American businesses this year.</p> \n<p>The amount of money spent on paid social media ads has been steadily climbing since 2019, and now, with businesses preparing to spend nearly a fifth of their ad budgets on this pay-to-play promo, it’s clear that social media ads are becoming a staple in marketing strategies across small and large businesses.</p> \n<p>Ultimately, paid social media helps with targeting audiences and driving sales just as organic social media does. The advantage to paying for this type of value? Speed to market, campaign sustainability, and good old fashioned message frequency.</p> \n<p>Organic social media traffic can take days to build due to the algorithms at work behind the scenes of the most popular social media sites. If you’re running a short campaign, that ramp up time can cost you visibility and leads. With paid social media, your campaign can get started with an extra boost at a speed that organic posts just can’t match. In addition to sustaining views, traffic, and engagement for as long as your credit card can stand, you’ll have the benefit of retargeting consumers with your ads to achieve an <a href=\"https://www.jonloomer.com/facebook-ad-frequency/\">advertisement frequency that you can control</a>.</p> \n<p>In this article, we’ll discuss what paid social media is, the components of a paid social media strategy, and the top social media platforms for running paid ads.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=8ba68133-b408-456b-a531-171a91d2b38e&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Access Now: Free Media Planning Template\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/8ba68133-b408-456b-a531-171a91d2b38e.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p></p> \n<p>Pay-per-click advertising, branded or influencer-generated content, and display ads are all examples of paid social media. You’ll know a paid social media advertisement when you see one based on the “sponsored” or “promoted” tag near the post.</p> \n<p>Every social media channel is different. Twitter offers short-form content, Instagram focuses heavily on visual content, Facebook has its own marketplace for shopping enthusiasts, and LinkedIn is the home of networking professionals.</p> \n<p>As such, paid social media on each platform differs, and should, depending on the campaign and audience.</p> \n<p>Here, we're going to explore some quick strategies that will help you decide how to use paid social to the benefit of your brand.</p> \n<p>Having a paid social media strategy can optimize a marketing budget that might not be substantial enough to promote a large brand through traditional media channels. If your business is working with a limited budget to reach hefty ROI goals, look no further. We've gathered the important things you’ll need to know about using paid social media ads.</p> \n<p>To create a paid social media strategy, you’ll want to start with two critical items: An objective and a budget.</p> \n<h3>Paid Social Media Strategy Objective</h3> \n<p>Setting the objective for your paid social media strategy gives your subsequent tactics a direction to work with and a goal to achieve. Think of this strategy as a road trip. You start your journey at your house with the goal of making it to your destination by a certain time. Paid social ads work the same way — your audience is starting their journey with your brand on their newsfeed and your goal is to lead them to the destination — a content offer on your website, an email subscription form, or even your social media profile itself.</p> \n<p>To establish where your audience is starting their journey, you’ll use filters, settings, and other criteria to narrow down your audience so that everyone you target is starting from a similar place. This doesn’t have to be a physical location (although it can be). You can target people by their age, their hobbies, and even their occupation.</p> \n<p>Once you have your starting point, it’s time to define your destination. Different social media ad platforms have their own conversion tools, but the end goal is almost always the same — get people to share their contact information with your business. You might do this with a form fill or a visit to a landing page on your website. Either one works to reach the destination, but <a href=\"https://www.wordstream.com/blog/ws/2019/02/14/facebook-lead-ads-vs-landing-pages\">depending on your business’s needs</a>, you might prefer one or the other.</p> \n<h3>Paid Social Media Strategy Budget</h3> \n<p>Paid social media advertising is one of the least expensive types of advertising available in the traditional and digital market. The pay-to-play model for these channels makes them flexible enough to target only the people your business wants to attract, therefore you only have to pay for those you have the ability to reach.</p> \n<p>Unlike TV or radio ads that are priced based on the length of the spot and the time the ads will air, social media ads are priced based on the length of the campaign and the potential number of impressions you'll be working toward with your ads. This gives these types of ads a much more favorable KPI to track — <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/cost-per-acquisition\">cost per acquisition</a> — as opposed to traditional ads that can only vaguely track cost per million impressions.</p> \n<p>Paid social media ads can start as low as $1 because of the bidding model and lottery system some platforms use to bring ads onto users’ newsfeeds. Spending for this type of advertising is virtually unlimited, but you can set a limit that will stop the campaign from spending more money than you’ve allowed.</p> \n<p>You’ll need to keep an eye on your credit card balance as you reach the spending limit you’ve set as these campaigns are programmed to stop running when the money runs out. That might sound helpful, but it can be annoying at best and detrimental to your campaign at worst. If you’re running a large campaign that needs a budget that exceeds the limit of your credit card, even just a few hours of downtime to pay the balance down can mean lost leads and momentum for your campaign. If your credit card needs to be paid in full each day due to a high spending limit you’ve set for the ad campaign, a lucky person or people on your team will have the honor of creating several expense reports for the duration of the campaign.</p> \n<p>To avoid this problem, consider raising the balance on your business credit card so that you have plenty of time to pay it off before the ads max it out, or try setting a lower daily spending limit for your campaign.</p> \n<p>Each paid social media platform has unique features that set it apart from competitors. However, there are three key characteristics of a converting paid ad that you’ll want your platform of choice to support: visual content, easy access to lead capture forms, and enough space to include enticing ad copy.</p> \n<h3>Facebook</h3> \n<p>When advertising on Facebook, it's a good idea to use <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/business/ads/ad-targeting\">Facebook Targeted Ads</a>. It’s the most robust ad platform available by far and that’s not for nothing. This feature is run on a <a href=\"https://medium.com/social-media-tips/how-does-facebook-ads-bidding-work-and-how-much-do-ads-cost-e8dab524d7b0\">bidding system</a> — a type of advertising buying process where advertisers bid on a number of ads based on their preferred target audience. Then, that bid will be put into a lottery for a chance to be picked and displayed to that audience. Facebook ads can narrow an audience down to just a few hundred people based on geography, interests, demographics, and more. And while that may not be beneficial for most large corporations, it can be the difference between a slow month and a sold out day for a small business.</p> \n<p>Other than the lottery, Facebook Ads lets you show advertisements to your customers based on their behavior. This is helpful because you can keep advertising to your existing Facebook customers based on what Facebook tells you about their use of the app.</p> \n<p>Using Facebook Ads helps you build new leads and generate brand awareness. Facebook provides reports and analytics that are perfect for experimenting with variables like post time and content type, so try using different ad formats and see what your audience engages with most.</p> \n<p style=\"font-weight: bold;\">Facebook Ad Example: <a href=\"http://networkforgood.com\">Network for Good</a></p> \n<p><img alt=\"Network for Good facebook ad on peer to peer fundraising checklist\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Paid%20Social%20Media%20Worth%20The%20Investment%3F-1.png?width=650&amp;name=Paid%20Social%20Media%20Worth%20The%20Investment%3F-1.png\" title=\"\" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\"></p> \n<p style=\"font-size: 12px; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://networkforgood.com/\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>Network for Good has a strong paid social media strategy and has for a few years. As a servant leader in several nonprofit organizations, I’m targeted often with their checklists, templates, and guides on Facebook. Here’s why this ad works:</p> \n<ol start=\"1\"> \n <li><strong>It keeps users on the platform.</strong> When a user clicks through to download the checklist, they’re not redirected to an external website. Facebook offers businesses the option for in-app form fills (that's a lot of words to say that users remain on Facebook while they convert on the ad.) That means the user doesn’t experience much disruption when they interact with the ad and can finish their Facebook session as soon as they’re done downloading the checklist.</li> \n <li><strong>There’s a prompt to drive conversation.</strong> There’s no question about what this ad wants me to do — download the Peer-to-Peer Fundraising Checklist. Simple, clear copy like this makes it easy for the user to convert on this ad because they don’t have to think about what their next step should be. They can either keep scrolling or download.</li> \n</ol> \n<p>For more information about running your own Facebook Ads that can convert just like this one, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-paid-ad-checklist?_ga=2.225195290.121387002.1580754077-940436819.1565181751\">check out this checklist</a> for lesser-known tips about running successful ad campaigns on this platform.</p> \n<h3>Twitter</h3> \n<p>As a consumer, paid ads on Twitter tend to sneak up on me. I barely know I'm looking at a sponsored tweet because they look so similar to regular tweets. As a marketer, this is fantastic news; it means more eyes on your ads because they're not as blatant as ads on other social channels.</p> \n<p>Why Twitter Ads? Well, Twitter reports having <a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/970920/monetizable-daily-active-twitter-users-worldwide/\">192 million monetizable daily users</a> (the number of people who can see your ad on any given day), and when using their Ad software, you can target your ad to a specific demographic.</p> \n<p style=\"font-weight: bold;\">Twitter Ad Example: <a href=\"https://www.thepennyhoarder.com/\">The Penny Hoarder</a></p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Paid%20Social%20Media%20Worth%20The%20Investment_-4.jpg?width=450&amp;name=Paid%20Social%20Media%20Worth%20The%20Investment_-4.jpg\" alt=\"The Penny Hoarder twitter ad featuring an image of a tennessee welcome sign\" width=\"450\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 450px;\"></p> \n<p style=\"font-size: 12px; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://partners.thepennyhoarder.com/9-money-moves-every-tennessean-needs-to-make-this-week/\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>As a Tennessee native, The Penny Hoarder can deduce that I might like seeing imagery and copy about my home state. <a href=\"https://business.twitter.com/en/help/campaign-setup/campaign-targeting/geo-gender-and-language-targeting.html\">Geographically targeted ads</a> can be successful for businesses in a broad market category — like The Penny Hoarder. Financial advice is applicable to anyone anywhere, but by positioning the content in a way that affects my life, I felt intrigued to click on the ad and learn more. Here’s why else this ad works:</p> \n<ol> \n <li><strong>It brings more traffic to this blog article.</strong> The <a href=\"https://partners.thepennyhoarder.com/9-money-moves-every-tennessean-needs-to-make-this-week/\">original article</a> was published in August 2020, but the continuous advertising on Twitter brings in more views than it might receive organically. Unlike Facebook, which has devised ways to <a href=\"https://blog.hootsuite.com/facebook-algorithm/\">keep people on the site longer</a>, Twitter allows users to visit the Penny Hoarder Website and read the article with just one click.</li> \n <li><strong>It’s visually appealing. </strong>Geography is just one way to evoke emotions and resonate with consumers in an ad. By framing this ad (and the article it’s promoting) with an identifier like Tennessee, people who live in the area or are from the area will instantly say “this has to do with me and my community — I need to care.”</li> \n</ol> \n<p>Twitter provides ad settings based on your budget —like how frequently your ad will be seen, where it will be seen, and the ad type to run. When you’re ready to run your social ads on this platform, Twitter offers <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-set-up-twitter-ads-campaigns\">different formats</a> for you to choose from based on your goals.</p> \n<h3>Instagram</h3> \n<p><a href=\"https://business.instagram.com/getting-started/\">84% of people discover new products on Instagram</a> — up from 64% just four years ago. With growth like this, it probably isn't a bad idea to pay for a spot in front of the <a href=\"https://datareportal.com/reports/digital-2020-october-global-statshot\">1.16 billion accounts</a> in the platform’s advertising reach.</p> \n<p>To run ads on Instagram, you’ll need a business profile — this allows you to set up an ecommerce store right on the app. (That’s a plus if you don’t have a website prepared to accept payments or if you’re testing out ecommerce for the first time.)</p> \n<p>Since Facebook owns Instagram, you’ll be running ads concurrently on both platforms and they're all managed on Facebook.</p> \n<p>Using Instagram Ads, you can choose an amount of ad spend that works for your budget starting as low as $1. This amount is tied to the timeline of the campaign and the size of your audience.</p> \n<p>I compare Instagram ads to filling up a gas tank — you get the amount of gas you pay for. On Instagram, your ad campaign runs during the amount of time you pay for.</p> \n<p style=\"font-weight: bold;\">Instagram Ad Example: <a href=\"https://www.aveeno.com/?utm_source=google&amp;utm_medium=cpc&amp;utm_campaign=GO-USA-ENG-PS-Aveeno-BC-BM-RN-Masterbrand-Core&amp;utm_content=Brand-General&amp;utm_term=%2Baveeno&amp;gclid=Cj0KCQjwi7yCBhDJARIsAMWFScPDbXnnTLzNzD2AUJMauJXgLIdFtfzzOK6df_aEpUV1ZGNZM9aofuEaAgLtEALw_wcB&amp;gclsrc=aw.ds&amp;\">Aveeno</a></p> \n<p style=\"font-size: 12px; text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/aveeno-min-1.png?width=450&amp;name=aveeno-min-1.png\" alt=\"Aveeno helathy looking skin ad with a bottle of aveeno lotion\" width=\"450\" style=\"width: 450px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"> <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/instagram-story-ads\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>Aveeno utilized Instagram's ad platform to target consumers with their product. The simple design is eye-catching without becoming overwhelming and distracting. Here's why it works:</p> \n<ol> \n <li><strong>It's visually appealing.</strong> The neutral colors and clean design draws our eyes to the product. (The pointing hand is a bonus that keeps our eye on the CTA — the shopping cart!)</li> \n <li><strong>The call to action is simple.</strong> One of the great features of Instagram ads is the ability to swipe up to see more about the product or make a purchase. When you're done, it's easy to close out of the Aveeno website and continue consuming other Instagram content.</li> \n</ol> \n<h3>LinkedIn</h3> \n<p>On LinkedIn, millions of professionals have found a wealth of professional connections, their dream job, or both. The platform lets you reach thousands of people in your industry including thought leaders, hiring managers, and decision-makers.</p> \n<p>Fortunately, as a marketer, LinkedIn’s paid ads let you reach those same individuals on behalf of your business.</p> \n<p>There are 740 million professionals on LinkedIn, and <a href=\"https://business.linkedin.com/marketing-solutions/ad-targeting\">four out of five</a> of them drive business decisions —like business purchase decisions. This is a B2B advertiser's dream come true. With the potential to reach 60 million decision-makers on the <a href=\"https://business.linkedin.com/marketing-solutions/audience\">most popular social platform for lead generation</a>, it's good to consider LinkedIn as an optimal platform for B2B advertising.</p> \n<img alt=\"Example of LinkedIn Ads settings\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Paid%20Social%20Media%20Worth%20The%20Investment%3F.png?width=650&amp;name=Paid%20Social%20Media%20Worth%20The%20Investment%3F.png\" title=\"\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a style=\"font-size: 12px;\" href=\"https://sproutsocial.com/insights/linkedin-ads-guide/\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: left;\">LinkedIn's targeted ads let you type in keywords and select audiences by category. So, if you're posting a job for a certain role, LinkedIn can help you find a pool of diverse candidates with relevant experience.</p> \n<p><strong>LinkedIn Ad Example:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.on24.com/\">ON24</a></p> \n<p><img alt=\"On24 LinkedIn ad about a webinar on the topic of the evolution of the buyers journey\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Paid%20Social%20Media%20Worth%20The%20Investment%3F-2.png?width=650&amp;name=Paid%20Social%20Media%20Worth%20The%20Investment%3F-2.png\" title=\"\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<p style=\"font-size: 12px; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/company/on24\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>On24 uses short and sweet copy to start a dialogue with its target audience. By focusing on business use cases for its product, the ON24 can position itself as a thought leader on the topic of buyer journeys to entice LinkedIn users to register for the event. Here’s why it works:</p> \n<ol start=\"1\"> \n <li><strong>It keeps users on the platform.</strong> Similar to Facebook, LinkedIn uses in-app form fills to make the exchange between businesses and LinkedIn users who register for the event. That way, after they’re done registering, they can continue seeking their next opportunity, networking, or engaging with other content creators.</li> \n <li><strong>There’s a prompt to drive the conversation.</strong> No matter how much money you spend on ads, there isn’t a way to buy engagement on those ads. Comments, likes, and shares still need to come organically which means the captions, copy, and headlines you choose for your ads should make the most of the limited space available. ON24 does a great job of this by asking a question that everyone has an answer to in the caption of this promoted post.</li> \n</ol> \n<p>You can also play around with ad formats on LinkedIn to find which one is most effective. To find out more about the ad types on LinkedIn —such as sponsored, message, text, and dynamic — check out our post about <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/linkedin-advertising-campaigns?_ga=2.191445162.121387002.1580754077-940436819.1565181751\">creating an awesome LinkedIn Ad campaign</a>.</p> \n<h2>Scaling Your Paid Social Media Strategy</h2> \n<p>When you put money behind a campaign, no matter how much or how little, you’ll want a sustainable ROI that shows the budget, effort, and resources you expended were all worth it. That ROI growth means you’ll be able to scale your campaigns in the future, and paid ads can fuel your success.</p> \n<p>Now that you have a solid understanding of the most popular paid social media ad platforms on the market, you’ll need to track all of your hard work to realize that ROI. The native platforms we mentioned earlier do offer reporting and analytics, but what happens when you run a campaign across several different social media sites? I’ll give you a hint — it gets very messy very quickly.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"HubSpot's free ad tracking software\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Paid%20Social%20Media%20Worth%20The%20Investment%3F-3.png?width=650&amp;name=Paid%20Social%20Media%20Worth%20The%20Investment%3F-3.png\" title=\"\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/ads?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/paid-social-media&amp;hubs_post-cta=HubSpot%E2%80%99s%20free%20ad%20tracking%20software%20\">HubSpot’s free ad tracking software </a>gives you one hub in which to manage all of your social media paid ads. That means you can report the success of your campaigns in just a few clicks rather than spending an entire day hunting down the information in each native platform. You’ll also have one source of truth for the combined total impressions, reach, and clicks. That’s paid social media at scale.</p> \n<h2>Investing in paid social media — the verdict is in.</h2> \n<p>It's easy to think ad spend is just for the big brands, but making informed purchase decisions benefits every business.</p> \n<p>The truth is, social media channels are making advertising accessible to large and small businesses alike. Once you learn how to plan, create, and position your ads to your target audience, you’ll have a much smoother time proving the ad campaign’s ROI to your stakeholders.</p> \n<p><em>Editor's note: This post was originally published in February 2020 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.</em></p> \n<p></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\"
