Marketing","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/benefits-high-quality-content-consistency-brand","description":"<p>In this competitive B2B marketing landscape, businesses make substantial investments in building content marketing programs.</p> \n<p>Why? Content marketing has been proven to deliver resounding success.</p>  \n<p>As one of the most effective methods of growing audience engagement, developing your brand presence, and driving sales, content marketing is a mission-critical growth method for most businesses.</p> \n<p>Below, let's review content marketing — the benefits of producing consistent, high-quality content, and how to measure success.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=2000ba0b-ea58-45a5-ac81-3b463d992c1a&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Download Now: Free Content Marketing Mapping Template\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/2000ba0b-ea58-45a5-ac81-3b463d992c1a.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p>According to the State of Inbound report, content creation is a<a href=\"https://www.stateofinbound.com/?__hstc=20629287.84e04411a062bd71ea6e407b66fb20f0.1607454300758.1616014513645.1616031476958.281&amp;__hssc=20629287.1.1616031476958&amp;__hsfp=3109495322\"> top priority for 53% of marketers.</a> Moreover, on average, content marketing accounts for<a href=\"https://www.pointvisible.com/blog/content-marketing-statistics-and-trends-2017/\"> 29% of B2B marketing budgets</a>.</p> \n<blockquote>\n Consistent, high-quality, and engaging content impacts audience decision-making more than any other technique.\n</blockquote> \n<p>Consistency in brand messaging is one of the many factors that determine the growth and success of your business. Big brands know how to portray their brand consistently and at every <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/service/customer-touchpoints\">customer touchpoint</a>.</p> \n<p>The same reasoning applies to content marketing — your content needs to carry a unique and identifiable voice, style, and pitch across all distribution channels.</p> \n<p>Content consistency establishes your credibility, builds trust, and strengthens your reputation.</p> \n<p>So, we know the content you create has to be consistent. However, why is content marketing so beneficial in the first place? Here are the top benefits of content marketing.</p> \n<h2>Benefits of Content Marketing</h2> \n<h3>1. Your audience will stick around longer.</h3> \n<p>Great content is an important asset. It has the ability to create positive experiences for your potential customers and compel them to come back for more. It's your ticket to capturing your audience's attention and continually reinforcing a positive brand impression.</p> \n<h3>2. You'll have better traction on social media.</h3> \n<p>It's one thing to increase your social media followers across channels, but it's quite another to create trendy content. If you're one of those businesses that doesn't see much traction despite having a huge following, it's time to use content marketing to your advantage. Quality content can help your business gain traction on social media.</p> \n<p>Track the performance of your content campaigns using <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/analytics?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/benefits-high-quality-content-consistency-brand&amp;hubs_post-cta=HubSpot%E2%80%99s%20analytics%20software\">HubSpot's analytics software</a>.</p> \n<h3>3. Your audience will trust you.</h3> \n<p>Creating content helps your business build a relationship with your audience. You can answer their questions and interact with customers. When you create value without taking anything in return, your audience is more likely to trust your advice and recommendations.</p> \n<p>Ultimately, when your content shows up at the right place and the right time with the right audience, it'll improve your brand's reputation.The more quality content customers see, the more likely they are to have a positive association with your company.</p> \n<h3>4. You'll generate more and better leads.</h3> \n<p>Content marketing can also generate leads. When your audience views your content, they're more likely to purchase from you in the future. Additionally, calls-to-action (CTA) placed directly in your content can generate new leads for your sales team.</p> \n<p>So, how can content generate leads?</p> \n<p>According to <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/beginner-inbound-lead-generation-guide-ht\">Lindsay Kolowich</a>, the team manager of the HubSpot Academy Acquisition Content Team, \"content is a great way to guide users to a landing page. Typically, you create content to provide visitors with useful, free information. You can include CTAs anywhere in your content — inline, bottom-of-post, in the hero, or even on the side panel. The more delighted a visitor is with your content, the more likely they are to click your call-to-action and move onto your landing page.\"</p> \n<h3>5. Original content can improve conversions.</h3> \n<p>The content you post influences conversions. It helps your audience connect with you and gives them information needed to make educated purchases.</p> \n<p>Even more, if you're using blog content to bring in traffic, consider using <a href=\"https://optinmonster.com/blogging-statistics/\">unique images rather than stock photos</a> for a potential 35% increase in conversions.</p> \n<p>Additionally, your content should always include a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/call-to-action-examples\">CTA</a> and guide your reader on what they should do next.</p> \n<h3>6. Your business will become more visible thanks to SEO.</h3> \n<p>The more consistent, high-quality content you produce, the better it'll be for your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/seo-strategy\">SEO efforts</a>.</p> \n<p>For example, your content should help your business become visible online and build trust and authority with your audience. With a developed content strategy, such as the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/pillar-cluster-model-transform-blog\">pillar/cluster model</a>, your content should help you rank higher in search engines.</p> \n<h3>7. Great content can position your company as an authority in your industry.</h3> \n<p>Creating quality content will also help build your authority online. If your business is established as a credible place to get information, you're more likely to rank higher in search engines.</p> \n<p>Plus, your customers are more inclined to trust you if they view you as an industry expert. Your content should demonstrate your expertise in your field and provide valuable answers to your audience's questions.</p> \n<p>Overall, content marketing is important. But, how can you be successful at it?</p> \n<p>One way to tell is to assess the quality of your content. One particularly beneficial assessment of quality is content scoring.</p> \n<p>As more businesses are <a href=\"https://www.brafton.com/blog/content-marketing/the-2020-state-of-content-marketing-report/#:~:text=Nearly%2050%25%20of%20B2B%20marketers,with%201%2D99%20employees%3A%20%24111%2C000\">increasing their content marketing budget</a>, there's never been a better time to incorporate content scoring metrics into your marketing campaign.</p> \n<p>With the help of content scoring, you can measure and improve your content marketing performance and offer great value to your audience.</p> \n<h3>8. Quality content can build brand awareness.</h3> \n<p>Sure, anything can build brand awareness, but content marketing can do it in a unique way.</p> \n<p>Our HubSpot marketing experts have written about something called <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/surround-sound-strategy-1\">Surround Sound strategy</a>.</p> \n<p>In a nutshell, this content strategy does more than just rank your blog article on page one. It makes your content (and therefore your brand) appear everywhere your potential customers are looking for your product.</p> \n<p>To execute this strategy, write about topics your customers are interested in so they begin to associate your great content with your brand.</p> \n<h3>9. You'll cultivate loyal brand fans.</h3> \n<p>Taking brand awareness a step further, all the people who raved about your content and associated all those great feelings to your brand are very likely to become brand advocates before ever purchasing your product.</p> \n<p>Wait, what?</p> \n<p>It's true, brand fans can be just as <a href=\"https://neilpatel.com/blog/customers-who-dont-convert/\">loyal and influence their friends' and family's buying decisions</a> as much as a current customer can. This happens when potential consumers see that a business provides value to its current audience. One of the more successful ways businesses can do this is through content marketing.</p> \n<p>For example, while I may not be in the market for children's meal plans because I don't have children yet, I am obsessed with the <a href=\"https://kidseatincolor.com/\">Kids Eat In Color</a> blog and Instagram content. I recommend it to my friends and family who have children with picky eating habits. See how well that can work?</p> \n<h3>10. You'll save money on your marketing strategy.</h3> \n<p>Since HubSpot <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/10172/inbound-leads-cost-62-less-than-outbound-new-data.aspx\">first assessed the cost of content marketing</a> ten years ago, the practice has remained the <a href=\"https://caliston.co.uk/blog/internet-marketing/5-cost-effective-marketing-strategies-for-2021\">most cost-effective marketing strategy</a> available.</p> \n<p>Upfront costs for content appear steep, and that's a fair point.</p> \n<p>Estimates for blog content range from $150 a post to $3,000 for a freelance writer, but you could go the route of hiring a full-time staff writer to create content for you on a regular basis.</p> \n<p>In the long term, when compared to paid advertisements, video marketing, and traditional marketing, content wins the battle with Frank from finance every time.</p> \n<h2>What is content scoring?</h2> \n<p>Content scoring is the process of assessing and quantifying the true potential of content by tracking how individual content pieces perform in generating and converting leads.</p> \n<p>As an innovative content marketing metric, content scoring helps marketers prioritize only the assets that have a higher probability of generating and converting leads.</p> \n<p>In addition to delivering a scientific method of assessment to writing, content scoring is a reliable and predictive method of evaluating the engagement potential of an individual piece of content before it's published.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-marketing-plan\">Improving the quality of your content</a> is pivotal to the success of your marketing campaigns.</p> \n<p>The quality of your content is relative to your audience's profile. With a better understanding of your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/service/customer-needs\">customer's needs</a>, you can offer content with higher resonance. But improving your content is a gradual process, and you need to continually measure and analyze your audience's responses to understand and improve on the elements that matter most.</p> \n<h2>How to Score Your Content</h2> \n<p>Writers and content creators often find it difficult to quantify what recipe works for their content and their audience. By scoring your content, you're able to objectify that process and use the same recipe repeatedly to create similarly successful content.</p> \n<p>Here's how to score your content:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Establish scoring criteria. To develop an effective content scoring system, you need to establish a foundation built on whichever engagement metric has the greatest impact on your content. For some, it may be page views, for others it could be shares on social media.</li> \n <li>Create a campaign. Once you've identified which metric matters to you most, create a campaign and add the successful content that meets your threshold. For example, if you decide that 1,000 page views is high performing, include all the content assets that meet said criteria.</li> \n <li>Monitor content performance. Measure how each new piece of content you create is performing. As certain content assets meet your success metric — 1,000 page views, for example — add them to the campaign. Continue adding content to build a small sample size of high-performing content. Use <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/analytics?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/benefits-high-quality-content-consistency-brand&amp;hubs_post-cta=HubSpot%20Analytics\">HubSpot Analytics</a> to track the performance of this content.</li> \n <li>Evaluate what works. Now that your high-performing content is segregated, you can further analyze what makes your content perform. Although it's difficult to quantify, you can discover patterns within your content that you can then replicate.</li> \n <li>Rinse and repeat. Although these patterns are always changing, this manual process is an effective way to score your content and take action on your insights in the future.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>This can be a tedious process, and it only scrapes the surface of a true content scoring system, but it's a thorough and important process to implement. For more effective and efficient results, you can use an automated tool like <a href=\"https://www.atomicreach.com/hubspot/index.html\">Atomic AI</a> to help you score your content in more granular patterns.</p> \n<p>Content scoring helps your brand set a benchmark for itself, moving you closer to understanding customer's buying stages and expectations. When you've established the content types that work for a specific customer segment, you can easily replicate your success over and over again.</p> \n<h2>Start Creating Consistent Content</h2> \n<p>Creating a content marketing strategy is one of the most important steps you can take for your marketing team. To do so, take an audit of your current content and figure out what works for your business.</p> \n<div>\n <em>Editor's note: This post was originally published in November 2017 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.</em>\n</div> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=dc23c777-516f-4c62-b371-70b180c87a3e&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 06 Apr 2021 11:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/2000ba0b-ea58-45a5-ac81-3b463d992c1a.png","linkMd5":"f48b0633cc12bf22e2e7c7df87fbabc6","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn52@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-07-747_0182497c26874791.webp","destWidth":522,"destHeight":59,"sourceBytes":6131,"destBytes":8284,"author":"Rebecca Riserbato","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/2000ba0b-ea58-45a5-ac81-3b463d992c1a.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn52@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-07-747_0182497c26874791.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/dc23c777-516f-4c62-b371-70b180c87a3e.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn71@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-14-955_d198dce450120884.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fbenefits-high-quality-content-consistency-brand&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn60@2020_6/2021/04/07/17-38-14-944_c09e6f666cdc5067.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817087121},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:07","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:07","title":"How to Embed a Facebook Feed On Your Website [Quick Tutorial]","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-feed-on-website","description":"<p>Facebook is an undeniably powerful channel for marketing purposes. In fact, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/social-network-advertising\">91% of B2B and 96% of B2C marketers</a>&nbsp;currently use it for advertising and marketing.</p> \n<p>The success of your social media marketing strategy depends on engagement, typically in the form of Likes, comments, or shares. But high engagement rates are easier said than done.</p> \n<p>One opportunity to increase engagement on your business' Facebook Page is by embedding your Page on your website — which could increase likes and comments on your posts <em>without</em>&nbsp;driving viewers away from your site.</p> \n<p>Here, we'll explore how to embed a Facebook feed on a website. Whether you host your website on HubSpot, WordPress, Squarespace, or Wix, we've got you covered.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=9f7c45b7-c71b-4797-8d5d-e6b296fb6a83&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Free Resource: How to Reach &amp; Engage Your Audience on Facebook\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/9f7c45b7-c71b-4797-8d5d-e6b296fb6a83.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: normal;\">How to Embed a Facebook Feed on a Website</span></h2> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: normal;\">1. HubSpot</span></h3> \n<p>If you want to embed a Facebook feed on your HubSpot-hosted site, it's incredibly easy to do.</p> \n<p><strong>1. First, go to </strong><strong><a href=\"https://developers.facebook.com/docs/plugins/page-plugin/\">Facebook's Plugin Page</a></strong><strong>. </strong></p> \n<p><strong>2. Copy-and-paste your business' Business Page into the \"Facebook Page URL\" box. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-45-10-PM.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-45-10-PM.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>3. Then, adjust the width and height to suit your preferences depending on your website and placement. Once you've adjusted the timeline, click the \"Get Code\" button. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>4. Switch to the IFrame tab, and copy the custom module. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-4.png?width=624&amp;height=240&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-4.png\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" height=\"240\"></p> \n<p><strong>5. Next, open the Editor tool on your HubSpot Landing Page, and select \"Source Code\". </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-2.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-2.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>6. Now, paste your IFrame code into the Source Code section of your page. Then click, \"Save Changes\". </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-44-20-PM.png?width=624&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-44-20-PM.png\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p>And voila! Your timeline is officially embedded on the HubSpot landing page of your choosing.</p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: normal;\">2. Squarespace</span></h3> \n<p>If you host your website on Squarespace, you're going to follow most of the instructions listed above. However, the third step varies for this website hosting platform.</p> \n<p>Let's explore how to embed a Facebook feed on Squarespace. It's important to note: Adding JavaScript or IFrames to Code Blocks is a <strong>Premium feature</strong>&nbsp;available in Business and Commerce plans, so you'll need a Premium account to proceed.</p> \n<p><strong>1. First, go to </strong><strong><a href=\"https://developers.facebook.com/docs/plugins/page-plugin/\">Facebook's Plugin Page</a></strong><strong>. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-44-41-PM.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-44-41-PM.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>2. Copy-and-paste your business Page URL into the \"Facebook Page URL\" box. Then, adjust the width and height to suit your preferences depending on your website and placement. </strong></p> \n<p><strong>Once you've adjusted the timeline, click the \"Get Code\" button. Copy the code in JavaScript form.&nbsp;</strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-44-62-PM.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-44-62-PM.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>3. Next, click \"Edit Post\" on a Squarespace page, then click an Insert point and choose \"Code\" from the menu:</strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-3.jpeg?width=624&amp;height=352&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-3.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" height=\"352\"></p> \n<p><strong>4. Next, choose Javascript from the dropdown menu, and then copy-and-paste your Facebook code into the box. Then click \"Apply\". </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-1.jpeg?width=624&amp;height=296&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-1.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" height=\"296\"></p> \n<p>If you have additional questions on adding unique code into your Squarespace page, take a look at <a href=\"https://support.squarespace.com/hc/en-us/articles/206543167\">Squarespace's Code Blocks FAQ page</a>.</p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">3. WordPress</h3> \n<p>WordPress varies slightly from the instructions listed above.</p> \n<p>Instead of using Facebook's custom code, you can use a WordPress plugin. (Note: You will need to upgrade to the Business plan on WordPress to use this plugin feature.)</p> \n<p>For our purposes, let's use this <a href=\"https://wordpress.org/plugins/custom-facebook-feed/\">Smash Balloon Social Post Feed plugin</a>, which is 5-star rated and has over 200,000 active installations.</p> \n<p>Before proceeding with the following steps, ensure you install the plugin on your Business plan WordPress account. You can install either via the WordPress plugin directory, or by uploading the files to your web server (in the /wp-content/plugins/ directory). Then click \"Activate\".</p> \n<p><strong>1. Navigate to the 'Facebook Feed' tab within WordPress to configure your feed. Then click \"Connect a Facebook account\" and choose your Business page. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-45-99-PM.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-45-99-PM.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>2. Next, copy the shortcode [custom-facebook-feed] to embed your feed on your site. (You can also display multiple feeds of different Facebook pages by specifying a Page ID directly in the shortcode: [custom-facebook-feed id=smashballoon num=5].)</strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-1.png?width=624&amp;height=96&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-1.png\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" height=\"96\"></p> \n<p><strong>3. Paste it into the body text on your new or existing WordPress page. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-44-92-PM.png?width=624&amp;height=232&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-44-92-PM.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" height=\"232\"></p> \n<p><strong>4. All set! Once you preview your page you'll see how the timeline looks in Live mode. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-45-48-PM.png?width=558&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-45-48-PM.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 558px;\" title=\"\" width=\"558\"></p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: normal;\">4. Wix</span></h3> \n<p>For Wix customers, you'll use a third-party tool — <a href=\"https://elfsight.com/\">Elfsight</a> — to create the unique code that you can use on your Wix website, which is why there are a few additional steps in this list.</p> \n<p><strong>1. Create your own Elfsight Apps account, or login to your existing account. (It's free to embed one Facebook feed code. If you need to use Elfsight often, consider the <a href=\"https://apps.elfsight.com/panel/all-apps-plans/\">Basic plan</a>, which is $18/month for startups and new businesses.)<br></strong></p> \n<p><strong>2. Click on the \"Facebook Feed\" application, under the Social Tab. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-4.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-4.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>3. Select the template you want to use, which will determine how your Facebook feed looks on your Wix site. For instance, you can choose to have a small-widget Facebook feed, or a full-screen Facebook feed. Click \"Continue with this template…\" when you're ready. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-2.png?width=624&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-2.png\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>4. Next, click the \"Connect to Facebook\" button to connect your business' Facebook Page with Elfsight. You can also click on the \"Layout\" tab to change the height and width of your widget.</strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-43-91-PM.png?width=624&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-43-91-PM.png\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>5. When you're ready, click \"Save\". A pop-up will appear that provides you with the code you need to embed your page on your Wix website. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<p><strong>6. Now, open your Wix ADI and select \"Add\" at the top of your Wix page. Click \"Section to Page\". </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-45-30-PM.png?width=624&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-45-30-PM.png\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>7. Choose \"HTML Embed\" in the navigation bar. </strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-45-76-PM.jpeg?width=624&amp;name=embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-45-76-PM.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: 0.00px;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\"></p> \n<p><strong>8. Now, click on the section design you prefer. Then fill in the title, subtitle, and paragraph. When you're ready, click the blue \"Settings\" button on HTML.</strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-43-42-PM.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<p><strong>9. Choose the embed type — in this case, you'll want \"HTML code\". Then, paste the HTML code you got from Elfsight into this section.&nbsp;</strong></p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-3.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<p><strong>10. Finally, click \"Publish\" on your Wix page to add your Facebook feed to your live Wix site. </strong></p> \n<h2 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">How to Embed Facebook Event Feed on Website</h2> \n<p>To embed a Facebook Event Feed on your website, go to the <a href=\"https://developers.facebook.com/docs/plugins/page-plugin/\">Page Plugin</a>&nbsp;and paste your Facebook Page URL into the box. Then, type \"events\" into the Tabs section.</p> \n<p>Now, click \"Get Code\" and copy-and-paste that code into your existing site using the steps outlined above. &nbsp;&nbsp;</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/post%20event%20feed%20on%20facebook.jpg?width=1236&amp;name=post%20event%20feed%20on%20facebook.jpg\" alt=\"post event feed on facebook\" width=\"1236\" style=\"width: 1236px;\">And there you have it! You're now ready to embed any post, timeline, or event onto your website to increase engagement to your social pages.&nbsp;</p> \n<p></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=b1ed53ce-abab-413f-b67a-846d53ac1657&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" %20on%20website-Mar-30-2021-02-42-43-42-PM.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn76@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-14-296_61aafbbf3515aca2.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/embed%20facebook%20feed%20on%20website-3.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn15@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-15-071_baa8b65e925abf59.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/post%20event%20feed%20on%20facebook.jpg?width=1236&name=post%20event%20feed%20on%20facebook.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn11@2020_6/2021/04/07/17-38-20-609_989aab24047f4c11.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b1ed53ce-abab-413f-b67a-846d53ac1657.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn99@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-14-472_43149526df2d3104.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Ffacebook-feed-on-website&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn4@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-14-982_58b24009e259ed84.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817087168},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:07","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:07","title":"Facebook Ads vs. Google Ads: Which is Better for Your Brand?","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-ads-vs-google-ads","description":"<p>If you're reading this article, it's likely because you're considering running digital ads.</p>  \n<p>You've heard about <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-paid-ad-checklist?_ga=2.262147973.848841103.1615582146-667627135.1615582146\">Facebook Ads</a> and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/google-adwords-ppc\">Google Ads</a> but you're still unclear on the difference between the two platforms.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=3242765b-a13a-461a-954d-510ce203b180&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"Free Guide, Template &amp; Planner: How to Use Google Ads for Business\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/3242765b-a13a-461a-954d-510ce203b180.png\"></a></p> \n<p>In this article, we'll cover each platform's unique features, the key differences to keep in mind, and the factors to consider when deciding which ad platform to use.</p> \n<p>Let's get started.</p> \n<p>These platforms are often pitted against each other but in fact, Facebook Ads and Google Ads are complementary, each offering unique benefits to marketers.</p> \n<p>If your team can only focus on one, there are a few things you'll want to consider.</p> \n<h3>Your Campaign Goal</h3> \n<p>What do you want to accomplish with your campaign? Is it brand awareness, leads, sales, or something else? Knowing this answer can already steer you in the right direction.</p> \n<p>Google Ads is ideal for demand capture – meaning reaching users who have high purchase intent. For instance, if I'm looking up the keyword \"water bottle,\" this may signal an interest in purchasing one.</p> \n<p>With that in mind, the ads below align well with search intent and can lead to sales.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Google search ad example\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Facebook%20Ads%20vs.%20Google%20Ads%20Which%20is%20better%20for%20your%20brand%3F-1.png?width=624&amp;height=272&amp;name=Facebook%20Ads%20vs.%20Google%20Ads%20Which%20is%20better%20for%20your%20brand%3F-1.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" height=\"272\"></p> \n<p>Facebook Ads, on the other hand, is ideal for reaching consumers who are near the top of <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-for-every-funnel-stage\">the funnel</a>, (i.e., great for brand and product awareness). <img alt=\"Facebook ad example\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Facebook%20Ads%20vs.%20Google%20Ads%20Which%20is%20better%20for%20your%20brand%3F.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\"></p> \n<p>So, you could use both platforms at the same time to target users at every stage of the journey. But if that doesn't align with your broader objectives, knowing the main goal of your campaign will help you determine which platform is better suited to achieve it.</p> \n<h3>Your Budget</h3> \n<p>With any ad campaign, your goal is to <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/return-on-ad-spend\">maximize your return on ad spend</a> (ROAS). It's easier to do that on some platforms than others.</p> \n<p>With Google Ads, you'll have to look at keyword competition and keyword price. If the keywords you're targeting have high cost-per-click (CPC) and you have a small budget, it may not be the best place for you to invest your money.</p> \n<p>For instance, let's say you have a $100 daily budget. You want to rank for \"hardware store\" in your local area but the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/google-ads-cost\">cost for that keyword</a> is $20. This means that you'd get a maximum five clicks per day – pretty limiting.</p> \n<p>With that same $100 budget, you could potentially reach more people on Facebook Ads and conduct experiments to learn more about which strategies work for your target audience.</p> \n<p>It's all about finding where your dollar will go the furthest in relation to your goals. Tools like <a href=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=http://hubspot.com/products/marketing/ads&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1615400695272000&amp;usg=AOvVaw2DcGFVACBt4BIGl4BGT4tU\">HubSpot's ads software</a> can help you measure your campaign's ROI and allow you to make adjustments to optimize its performance.</p> \n<h3>Stages in the Buyer's Journey</h3> \n<p>As mentioned above, certain platforms align better with certain stages in the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/what-is-the-buyers-journey\">buyer's journey</a>.</p> \n<p>With Facebook being a social media platform, most users are not actively looking to purchase products. However, they do explore and share their interests on the platform. With that in mind, it's a great place for users to discover your brand, especially if you don't think it relates to a topic users will be searching.</p> \n<p>In contrast, it's estimated that Google receives over 5 billion searches every single day. These searches can fall anywhere on the buyer's journey stage, but certain keywords indicate a high purchase intent.</p> \n<p>For example, if I search \"best water bottle\" or \"water bottle price,\" this suggests that I am interested in purchasing this item. With this approach, marketers can reach users they <em>know</em> are near the bottom of the funnel.</p> \n<h3>Historical and/or Competitor Data</h3> \n<p>As you develop your playbook for your next campaign, it will be helpful to look at historical data to inform your strategy. Knowing what has worked in the past, what hasn't and what is left to explore can serve as a reference and benchmark.</p> \n<p>If you've never run a campaign before, look at your competitors. What ads are they running? Where are they running them? What do their creative assets look like? What's their messaging?</p> \n<p>This <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/competitive-intelligence-competitive-advantage\">competitive intel </a>may highlight some areas for opportunity and give you insight into the strategies your competitors are using.</p> \n<h2>Benefits of Facebook Ads</h2> \n<p>In a <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/state-of-marketing\">2019 HubSpot State of Marketing Report</a>, marketers revealed that the paid channel offering the highest ROI was Facebook. Let's dive into some of the reasons why.</p> \n<p>For starters, Facebook is the number one social media platform with over 2.7 billion monthly active users, according to a <a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/272014/global-social-networks-ranked-by-number-of-users/\">2021 Statista report</a>. In addition to its large audience base, the platform offers granular targeting capabilities, allowing marketers to reach users based on demographics, behaviors, life events and interests.</p> \n<p>Before launching a campaign on the platform, you can create a \"<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-lookalike-audiences\">lookalike audience</a>,\" which is essentially your<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/buyer-persona-research\"> user persona.</a> Facebook Ads will then show your ads to audiences who match your description.</p> \n<p>That's one advantage the platform has over Google Ads – it's much more detailed in who you're able to target for your ads.</p> \n<p>Beyond that, you may also be able to reach more users and get a better clickthrough rate (CTR) through Facebook Ads. <a href=\"https://www.smartinsights.com/internet-advertising/internet-advertising-analytics/display-advertising-clickthrough-rates/\">Smart Insights reported</a> found that in Q1 of 2020, the median CTR for a Facebook ad on the newsfeed was 1.11% – compared to .47% for Google Display ads in the same time period.</p> \n<h2>Benefits of Google Ads</h2> \n<p>In 2019, <a href=\"https://economicimpact.google.com/methodology/\">Google estimated</a> that for every dollar a business spends on ads, it earns $8 in profit. Let's see why that may be and how the platform can be useful for brands.</p> \n<p>Google Ads, formerly known as Google Adwords, initially offered only very simple text-based ads on the search engine. Now, it's evolved to include features that can drastically improve clickthrough rates, such as reviews, detailed contact information, a shopping function, and mobile optimization.</p> \n<p>In Q1 of 2020, <a href=\"https://www.smartinsights.com/internet-advertising/internet-advertising-analytics/display-advertising-clickthrough-rates/\">Smart Insights</a> found that Google search ads had the highest CTR at 1.55% when compared to display ads and Facebook ads. This is likely because Google prioritizes ads based on relevance.</p> \n<p>While you do have to bid on keywords, the highest bid doesn't necessarily always win. Your bid gets your foot in the door, your ad's relevance to the keyword the user's search intent gets you in the house.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/design-content-remarketing-campaigns\">Remarketing</a>, which is reconnecting with users who have interacted with your brand before, is now much easier using Google Ads. So, let's say someone visited your site and added something to their shopping cart but didn't complete their purchase. You can now re-engage users as they search on Google, watch a YouTube video or navigate a site within Google's Display Network.</p> \n<p>In addition, the platform's simple interface and advanced features like search term report, ads editor and auction insights make it easy to <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/marketing-campaigns\">build, launch and track campaigns</a>.</p> \n<p>With Facebook Ads and Google Ads, one isn't inherently better than the other. Once you account for your goals, budget and target audience, you will find that each one offers unique features that can be useful to your brand at various points in its growth.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=c5cea574-dc9b-436a-8cc5-0d208bf2cbd9&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"New Call-to-action\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/c5cea574-dc9b-436a-8cc5-0d208bf2cbd9.png\"></a></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Ffacebook-ads-vs-google-ads&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 06 Apr 2021 11:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/3242765b-a13a-461a-954d-510ce203b180.png","linkMd5":"9b5b69a05a449fa57828b6ae5021ebca","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn72@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-07-840_37786f1e2b3f2dfc.webp","destWidth":630,"destHeight":60,"sourceBytes":5566,"destBytes":9538,"author":"mbretous@hubspot.com (Martina Bretous)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/3242765b-a13a-461a-954d-510ce203b180.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn72@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-07-840_37786f1e2b3f2dfc.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Facebook%20Ads%20vs.%20Google%20Ads%20Which%20is%20better%20for%20your%20brand%3F-1.png?width=624&height=272&name=Facebook%20Ads%20vs.%20Google%20Ads%20Which%20is%20better%20for%20your%20brand%3F-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn81@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-14-107_6a861cf8883970a6.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Facebook%20Ads%20vs.%20Google%20Ads%20Which%20is%20better%20for%20your%20brand%3F.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn39@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-21-239_a733987cbfa18858.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/c5cea574-dc9b-436a-8cc5-0d208bf2cbd9.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn16@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-14-543_c90fcbcd44a0eec6.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Ffacebook-ads-vs-google-ads&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn77@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-33-792_f8fb3bc28959ef7c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817087131},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:07","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:07","title":"A Marketer's Quick Guide to Dynamic Ads","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/dynamic-ads","description":"<p>Remember when you'd go to the mall, see something you liked, but then leave without it? Then you’d leave the mall and think about it the whole drive home, wondering if you made the right decision until you forgot about it. That was until you saw someone else with the exact item we wanted. Ah, the good ol’ days.</p> \n<p>Today, you can’t leave an item in your cart without it following you <em>everywhere</em> online. Who do we have to thank for that? Technically, a lot of people – marketers, retargeting tools, Al Gore’s internet – but for the purpose of this article, we’ll focus on one: dynamic ads.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=da1bfbbd-7ee9-4bf1-89d1-6d7a833deb08&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"Download Now: Free Ad Campaign Planning Kit\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/da1bfbbd-7ee9-4bf1-89d1-6d7a833deb08.png\" /></a></p> \n<p>Dynamic ads allow brands to change the ads shown to users based on their behavior.</p> \n<p>Let’s dive into what exactly dynamic ads are, their benefits, and how to use them on social media platforms like <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/linkedin-content-marketing\">LinkedIn</a> and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-paid-ad-checklist\">Facebook</a>.</p> \n<p>Dynamic ads are often used in <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/design-content-remarketing-campaigns\">remarketing campaigns </a>to reach users who have already interacted with a brand. More on that <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/dynamic-ads#remarketing\">here</a>.</p> \n<p>Static ads, on the other hand, do not adapt based on external data, so they tend to target broader audience groups for brand awareness or product launches.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/banner-ad-clicks\">A banner ad</a> can look like this:</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/dynamic-ad-website-example.jpg?width=300&amp;name=dynamic-ad-website-example.jpg\" alt=\"banner ad example\" width=\"300\" style=\"width: 300px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\">Or like this:</img></p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/dynamic-ad-facebook-example.jpg?width=300&amp;name=dynamic-ad-facebook-example.jpg\" alt=\"banner ad example on facebook\" width=\"300\" style=\"width: 300px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> \n<p>They range in size and placement depending on the platform on which they’re displayed.</p> \n<h2>The Benefits of Dynamic Ads</h2> \n<p>Ad personalization is one of the biggest advantages of using dynamic banner ads. In a <a href=\"https://info.innovid.com/2020-consumer-attitudes\">2020 study by Innovid</a>, 43% of respondents agreed that ads should be personalized.</p> \n<p>What’s more, 30% of respondents said they liked brands more when ads were personalized. It’s easy to understand why – there’s nothing more annoying than getting an irrelevant ad that doesn’t relate to you or your interests. In fact, it’s a major reason why people get adblockers.</p> \n<p>In 2020, <a href=\"https://www.audienceproject.com/resources/insight-studies/attitude-towards-advertising-and-use-of-ad-blocking-2/\">AudienceProjects surveyed</a> people in the US, UK, Denmark, Sweden, Norway, and Finland and found that avoiding offensive or irrelevant ads was the second most popular reason why they got adblockers.</p> \n<p>The more personalized the ad, the better the chances it will resonate with the audience. This brings us to the next benefit of dynamic ads: relevance.</p> \n<p>While an ad may be personalized, it may not be relevant to that user’s current stage in the buyer’s journey.</p> \n<p>For instance, imagine you’ve heard of a brand but aren’t exactly sure what they do or what they offer. Getting an ad to request a product demo may be too big of a jump. You may need more nurturing before you reach that level of interest in their products.</p> \n<p>With this in mind, dynamic ads can help you only present ads that will meet the user where they are. Doing so can move them further down the funnel and help generate more revenue for your brand.</p> \n<p>This brings us to return on investment (ROI). Because of the reasons outlined above, your dynamic ads can optimize your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/return-on-ad-spend\">return on ad spend</a> (ROAS) because they are more targeted and relevant to each user.</p> \n<h2>How Dynamic Search Ads Work</h2> \n<h3>What are dynamic search ads?</h3> \n<p>Dynamic search ads (DSAs) are dynamic ads that show up on search engines like Google and Bing based on the content of your website, not keywords.</p> \n<p>When marketers set up <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/search-engine-marketing\">search campaigns</a>, they bid on specific keywords and create ads that match the intent behind the keywords. For instance, let’s say you’re a website operations company and you want to rank for the keyword \"best WebOps platforms,\" you’ll need to bid on it and win to show up on the search engine when a user searches that keyword.</p> \n<p>With dynamic search ads, you don’t have to bid on the keywords. The search engine will analyze the user’s search query and scan your website for relevant content. If the search engine determines it’s a match for what the user is looking for, it will automatically generate the ad with a headline and text based on a relevant landing page from your website.</p> \n<p>The main benefit of using DSAs is that it allows marketers to target audiences who may fall outside of the keywords they’re already targeting in their campaign.</p> \n<p>Think of a dynamic search as a safety net; even a well-designed search campaign won’t target all of the keywords your user persona might search for. The dynamic ad identifies new targeting opportunities and fills that gap by aligning your content with the right users – earning you extra traffic and more reach.</p> \n<p>It’s also a time-saver. With dynamic ads, you don’t have to go through the process of mapping out keywords, setting up bids, and creating copy for every single ad.</p> \n<p>My latest browsing sessions have involved a lot of furniture and home decor websites. This is why my Facebook feed includes ads like this:</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/facebook-dynamic-ad.jpg?width=400&amp;name=facebook-dynamic-ad.jpg\" alt=\"Dynamic Display Ad example on Facebook\" width=\"400\" style=\"width: 400px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\">And why I see ads like this when browsing online.</img></p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/website-dynamic-ad.jpg?width=500&amp;name=website-dynamic-ad.jpg\" alt=\"Dynamic Display Ad on website\" width=\"500\" style=\"width: 500px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\">They work just as regular dynamic ads do, adapting their content to the user for better results.</img></p> \n<p>You can take your display ads one step further by creating responsive dynamic display ads. It’s a mouthful, I know but the concept is simple to understand: A responsive ad adjusts its size based on the space on the page.</p> \n<p>For example, you’re on a website and you minimize the page to make space for another window. A responsive ad would adapt its shape based on that new space – just like a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/responsive-design-list\">responsive website</a>.</p> \n<p>This creates a better user experience and ensures your ad will be displayed correctly no matter the screen size.</p> \n<a></a> \n<h2>Dynamic Remarketing Ads</h2> \n<p>Let’s say I visit the <a href=\"https://sabai.design/\">Sabai Design</a> website to look at furniture. Then, I put a beautiful emerald green couch in my cart but don’t complete the purchase.</p> \n<p>If the brand sets up dynamic remarketing ads, I’d see that couch, and similar styles, as I’m scrolling through social media or browsing through websites over the next few days or weeks<em>. </em></p> \n<p>The way dynamic remarketing works is by pulling the product feed from your website and leveraging user data to show your visitors ads that will move them down your funnel.</p> \n<p>You can target various ad groups, ranging from visitors who’ve only visited your product pages to those who have already purchased items from you.</p> \n<p>Then, once you generate the ad copy and the offers, the ad platform you use will do the rest. This means pulling the relevant product information to show that specific user.</p> \n<h2>LinkedIn Dynamic Ads</h2> \n<p>When creating a dynamic <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/linkedin-advertising-campaigns\">ad on LinkedIn</a>, you will target users based on their profile, including demographics such as location, work experience, company, and job title.</p> \n<p>There are three main formats to use when creating ads on the professional network:</p> \n<h3>Follower Ads</h3> \n<h3 style=\"color: #434343; font-size: 14px;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/linkedin-dynamic-follower-ad.jpg?width=225&amp;name=linkedin-dynamic-follower-ad.jpg\" alt=\"LinkedIn Dynamic Follower Ad\" width=\"225\" style=\"width: 225px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\">If you want to gain more followers on your LinkedIn Company Page, create a Follower Ad. This will encourage users in your ad group to follow your Page and learn more about your brand.</img></h3> \n<h3>Spotlight Ads</h3> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/linkedin-dynamic-spotlight-ad.jpg?width=225&amp;name=linkedin-dynamic-spotlight-ad.jpg\" alt=\"LinkedIn Dynamic Spotlight Ad\" width=\"225\" style=\"width: 225px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> \n<p>Want to drive traffic to your website or landing page? Use a spotlight ad. You can also use it to promote upcoming events, highlight your products or services, or gain new email subscribers.</p> \n<h3>Content Ads</h3> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/linkedin-dynamic-content-ad.jpg?width=225&amp;name=linkedin-dynamic-content-ad.jpg\" alt=\"LinkedIn Dynamic Content Ad\" width=\"225\" style=\"width: 225px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\">Content offers are great <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/lead-generation-strategy\">lead magnets</a>. This dynamic ad format allows you to generate leads through downloadable offers. You can manage those leads in the LinkedIn Campaign Manager or export them to a CRM like the HubSpot <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/ads\">Marketing Hub’s Ads Software</a>.</img></p> \n<p>You’ll notice that none of these ads show up as a carousel image, single image ad, video, or text ad. That’s because dynamic ads on LinkedIn are only formatted to show up on the right sidebar on desktop view. Like this:</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/LinkedIn-dynamic-ad.jpg?width=500&amp;name=LinkedIn-dynamic-ad.jpg\" alt=\"LinkedIn Dynamic Ad Example\" width=\"500\" style=\"width: 500px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" /></p> \n<h2>Facebook Dynamic Ads</h2> \n<p>On Facebook, things work a little differently. In this case, dynamic ads are ideal for brands with a large inventory of products and/or services. Unlike LinkedIn ads, when creating a dynamic ad on Facebook, you can choose any ad format, including single image, carousel, stories, or collection.</p> \n<p>Here’s how Facebook dynamic ads work: You can create a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/the-facebook-ad-types\">retargeting campaign</a> to reach consumers who’ve had previous interactions with your brand, or reach a broader audience that matches your user persona and may be interested in your products or services.</p> \n<p>To set up a dynamic ad on Facebook, you’ll need:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>A catalog </strong>– This contains the products and services you want to promote, with descriptions, prices, images, availability, and other relevant information.</li> \n <li><strong>Facebook pixel or DSK</strong> – You must install a Facebook pixel on your website or SDK for your mobile app to capture how your users are behaving on your webpages or app.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>From there, you will set up your campaign in the Ads Manager to outline your ad objectives, ad format, copy, and calls-to-action (CTA) by product set.</p> \n<p>Every time a user fits your targeting parameters, the machine learning program will use the pixel to gather user data and pick relevant products or services from your catalog to display the ad on mobile, tablet, or desktop.</p> \n<p>This saves marketers time, as they don’t have to create an ad for every single product or ad group.</p> \n<p>You may no longer need those drives home from the mall to decide if you <em>really</em> should have bought something. With dynamic ads, you get multiple chances to reconsider your decisions.</p> \n<p>Whether that’s a good thing varies from person to person, but from a marketing standpoint, it’s another opportunity to win over a consumer. Why not take it?</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=46d72524-f4a7-44e9-9af0-935be9bb3891&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"advertising plan\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/46d72524-f4a7-44e9-9af0-935be9bb3891.png\" /></a></p> \n<p></p> \n<img
